The Maxim of Attributing an Event to the Nearest Time
Explaining the maxim with examples and exceptions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the maxim 'الأصل إضافة الحادث إلى أقرب أوقاته' to sales and option disputes, and identify the exception when it would negate an established fact.

Core Idea
When an event's timing is disputed, attribute it to the nearest agreed time unless this uproots a settled matter.

This lesson introduces a foundational legal maxim from the Hanafi school: the default rule for disputes about when an event occurred is to attribute it to the nearest time on which both parties agree. The rationale is certainty versus doubt. We will explore two concrete applications in sales and options, and examine the important exception that preserves established facts.

Guided Path
1
State the maxim
Recite the maxim in Arabic: 'الأصل إضافة الحادث إلى أقرب أوقاته' and its English translation: 'The principle is attributing an event to its nearest time.' Grasp the core idea that when timing is disputed, the default is the nearest time.
The maxim is Article 11 of the Majalla.
2
Understand the rationale
The nearest time is certain because both parties agree the event occurred then; an earlier time is doubtful because only one party claims it. Certainty prevails over doubt, so the event is placed at the nearest time.
Based on the principle 'اليقين لا يزول بالشك'.
3
Apply to sale defect case
If a defect appears after purchase, the default is that it occurred with the buyer (nearest time). The buyer cannot rescind unless he proves it existed with the seller.
Exception: if the defect is congenital, it is pre-existing.
4
Apply to option case
If a buyer claims cancellation within the option period after it expired, the default is that cancellation occurred after expiry. The seller's word is accepted; the buyer must prove early cancellation.
Burden of proof on the one claiming the earlier time.
5
Recognize the exception
The maxim is restricted: it does not apply when attributing to the nearest time would negate an established fact, such as a congenital defect. The governing maxim then is 'الأصل بقاء ما كان على ما كان'.
General exception: 'مالم تؤد هذه الإضافة إلى نقض أمر ثابت'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
هـ - «الأصل إضافة الحادث إلى أقرب أوقاته (م(۱۱). كثيراً ما تختلف أحكام الحوادث ونتائجها باختلاف تاريخ حدوثها. فعند التنازع في تاريخ الحادث يحمل على الوقت الأقرب إلى الحال حتى يثبت الأبعد. لأنَّ الوقت الأقرب قد اتفق الطرفان على وجود الحادث فيه، وانفرد أحدهما بزعم وجوده قبل ذلك. فوجود الحادث في الوقت الأقرب متيقن، وفي الأبعد مشكوك (من شرح والدي رحمه الله على القواعد). وعليه فروع كثيرة : منها ما لو تبين في المبيع عيب بعد القبض، فزعم البائع حدوثه عند المشتري، وزعم المشتري وجوده عند البائع ، فإنه يُعتبر حادثاً عند المشتري، فليس له فسخ البيع حتى يثبت أنه قديم عند البائع، إلا أن يكون العيب مما لا يحدث مثله، بل هو من أصل الخلقة، كالخَيْف في الفرس (1): (1) الخَيَف (بفتحتين) أن تكون إحدى العينين سوداء والأخرى زرقاء والوصف منه أخيف، وزان (أبيض وأسود). وكذا لو اشترى شخص شيئاً على أنه بالخيار مدة معينة، ثم جاء يرده بعد انقضاء مدة الخيار زاعماً أنه قد فسخ البيع قبل انقضائها، وزعم البائع أن المدة قد انقضت وهو ساكت فلزم البيع، وأنه قد فسخ بعد انقضائها. فالمعتبر في هذه قول البائع ولا يحق للمشتري الرد حتى يثبت أنه قد فسخ في مدة الخيار. هذا، وإنَّ لهذه القاعدة مستثنيات كثيرة لأنها مقيدة في نظر الفقهاء بأن الحادث إنما يضاف إلى أقرب أوقاته مالم تؤد هذه الإضافة إلى نقض أمر ثابت . (ر) شرح المجلة للعلامة علي حيدر تحت هذه القاعدة).
The principle is attributing an event to its nearest time (Article 11). Often the rulings of events and their consequences differ according to the time of their occurrence. So when there is a dispute over the time of an event, it is attributed to the time nearest to the present until the more distant is proven. Because the nearest time is agreed upon by both parties to contain the event, while one party claims its existence earlier. So the existence of the event in the nearest time is certain, while in the more distant it is doubtful (from my father's commentary on the rules). And there are many branches of this: among them, if a defect appears in the sold item after possession, and the seller claims it occurred with the buyer, while the buyer claims it existed with the seller, then it is considered to have occurred with the buyer, so he does not have the right to rescind the sale until he proves it was old with the seller, unless the defect is not of a type that occurs, but rather is of original creation, like al-khayaf in a horse (1): (1) al-khayaf means one eye black and the other blue, the adjective is akhyaf, like abyad and aswad. Similarly, if someone buys something with the option for a specified period, then comes to return it after the option period claiming he canceled before its expiry, while the seller claims the period expired while he was silent so the sale was confirmed, and that he canceled after its expiry. Then the seller's statement is considered, and the buyer does not have the right to return until he proves he canceled within the option period. This, and this rule has many exceptions because in the view of the jurists it is restricted: an event is attributed to its nearest time as long as this attribution does not lead to the negation of an established matter.
Source pages p. 919

Commentary
This passage presents the maxim 'الأصل إضافة الحادث إلى أقرب أوقاته'. It governs disputes about the time of events. The reasoning is based on certainty: the nearest time is certain (both agree it occurred), while an earlier time is doubtful. Therefore, the default is to attribute the event to the nearest time. Two applications are given: a hidden defect in a sale, and exercise of an option. Important exceptions exist: if attributing to the nearest time would contradict an established fact, then it is not applied. The exception is illustrated by the congenital defect example – since such a defect cannot arise after purchase, it is attributed to the seller.

Key Terms
الحادث (al-hadith): An event whose time of occurrence is disputed.
أقرب الأوقات (aqrab al-awqat): The nearest time to the present regarding which both parties agree the event occurred.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A buyer finds a defect in a horse after taking possession. The seller claims the defect occurred after possession. The buyer claims it existed before. According to the maxim, what is the default ruling?
A) The defect is attributed to the seller unless he proves otherwise
B) The defect is attributed to the buyer unless he proves otherwise
C) The sale is automatically rescinded
D) The horse is returned regardless

Key Takeaway
The maxim attributes disputed events to the nearest time, but this is overridden if it would contradict a certainty.

لا يُنسب إلى ساكت قول: When Silence Speaks in Hanafi Law
Expansion of maxim with furuat and istithna

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the maxim 'لا يُنسب إلى ساكت قول' to determine when silence has legal effect across different fiqh chapters, and identify the istithna' for close relatives.

Core Idea
Silence is not speech unless context forces a response — then silence speaks volumes.

This lesson unpacks one of the most practical maxims in Hanafi law: 'لا يُنسب إلى ساكت قول' (No speech is attributed to a silent person). But the maxim is not absolute — it carries an exception based on istihsan for close relatives, and it defines a key concept: 'معرض الحاجة' (situation that requires explanation). Understanding these contours is essential for a mufti who must discern when silence is legally binding.

Guided Path
1
State the Maxim and Its Rationale
Start with the maxim: silence is not speech because the absence of words is certain, whereas the meaning of silence is doubtful. This gives the default ruling.
The maxim is from the Majalla (article 57).
2
Identify the Default Rule with a Concrete Example
Apply the default: if someone sees his property being sold by another and stays silent, he can still reclaim it. Silence is not consent.
No close relationship — general rule applies.
3
Recognize the Exception for Close Relatives
When the seller is a spouse or close relative, silence is considered acknowledgment. This is based on istihsan to prevent manipulation.
The exception relies on the close relationship as a strong circumstantial evidence.
4
Define 'معرض الحاجة'
Silence is treated as speech only when the context demands a response to avoid harm or deception, or when custom so dictates.
This includes court proceedings, pre-emption, and marriage consent.
5
Apply to the Furuat from the Text
Walk through each furu' case: defendant's silence in court, pre-emptor's silence, virgin girl's silence in marriage. Identify why each falls under the rule or exception.
This builds practical application skill.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
13/81 - ز - لا يُنسب إلى ساكت قول، ولكن السكوت معرض الحاجة إلى البيان بيان (م/٥٧).
لأن عدم القول هو المتيقن ودلالة السكوت مشكوك فيها ما لم تدعمها قرائن مرجحة:
فلو رأى الشخص بعض ماله في يد غيره يبيعه وظل ساكتاً، كان له أن يدعي به بعد ذلك، ولا يعتبر سكوته عند البيع اعترافاً بالملكية للبائع، ولا إجازة للبيع. (1) هذا ما لم يكن البائع زوجاً أو قريباً محرماً من الشخص المدعي. فإن كان البائع زوجاً أو قريباً يعتبر سكوت زوجه أو قريبه عند البيع اعترافاً منه بأنه لا حق له في المبيع. وهذا استحسان منعاً للتلاعب والتغرير بواسطة الأقارب، ولأن الخلطة بينهما قرينة تجعل من سكوته اعترافاً بنفاذ البيع والقياس عدم الفرق بين القريب والغريب.
·
وكذلك لو سكتت زوجة العِنّين سنين لا يكون سكوتها رضاً مسقطاً حقها في التفريق القضائي بينها وبين زوجها.
والمراد بمعرض الحاجة الذي يكون فيه السكوت في حكم البيان والتعبير : كل موطن يلزم فيه التكلم لدفع ضرر أو غرر، أو يكون فيه السكوت طريقة عرفية للتعبير. وعلى هذا:
أ - لو سأل القاضي المُدَّعى عليه عما يقول في دعوى المدعي، فاعتصم بالسكوت يعتبر منكراً للدعوى فيكلف المدعي الإثبات. وإذا عجز عن الإثبات وطلب التحليف فعرضت اليمين على المدعى عليه، فسكت أيضاً دون أن يحلف أو ينكل، يعتبر ناكلاً عن اليمين ويقضي عليه، لأن توقف سير المحكمة على كلامه يضر المدعي .
ب - وكذا لو علم الشفيع ببيع العقار الذي له فيه حق الشفعة، فسكت عن طلبها، يُعتبر سكوته تسليماً مُسقطاً لشفعته، كي لا يعمد الشفيع إلى تغرير المشتري بهذا السكوت حتى يبني أو يغرس؛ ثم يطلب الشفيع أخذ العقار.
ج - ولو سكتت الفتاة البكر عند استئذان وليها لها بالتزويج، أو زوجها الولي دون استئذانها ثم بلغها العقد فسكتت، اعتبر سكوتها إذناً في الحالة الأولى، وإجازة في الثانية لدلالة الحال، كما تقدم بيانه في مناسبات عدة
13/81 - Z - No speech is attributed to a silent person, but silence in a situation that requires explanation is considered a statement (M/57). Because the absence of speech is certain and the indication of silence is doubtful unless supported by corroborating evidence. If a person sees some of his property in the hand of another selling it and remains silent, he has the right to claim it afterwards, and his silence at the time of sale is not considered an acknowledgment of ownership for the seller, nor a ratification of the sale. (1) This is unless the seller is a spouse or a close relative of the claimant. If the seller is a spouse or relative, the silence of the spouse or relative at the time of sale is considered an acknowledgment that he has no right in the sold item. This is istihsan to prevent manipulation and deception by relatives, and because the close relationship between them is a circumstantial evidence that makes his silence an acknowledgment of the validity of the sale, while by analogy there is no difference between a relative and a stranger. · Similarly, if the wife of an impotent man remains silent for years, her silence is not consent that drops her right to judicial separation between her and her husband. What is meant by 'a situation that requires explanation' in which silence is equivalent to explanation and expression is: every context in which speech is necessary to repel harm or deception, or in which silence is a customary method of expression. Accordingly: a) If the judge asks the defendant what he has to say about the plaintiff's claim, and he remains silent, he is considered to be denying the claim, so the plaintiff is required to provide proof. If he is unable to prove and requests an oath, and the oath is presented to the defendant, and he remains silent without swearing or refusing to swear, he is considered to have refused the oath and judgment is issued against him, because stopping the court proceedings on his speech harms the plaintiff. b) Similarly, if the pre-emptor learns of the sale of the property in which he has a right of pre-emption, and remains silent in requesting it, his silence is considered a forfeiture that drops his pre-emption right, so that the pre-emptor cannot deceive the buyer by this silence until he builds or plants, and then the pre-emptor demands taking the property. c) And if an unmarried virgin girl remains silent when her guardian seeks her permission for marriage, or the guardian marries her without seeking her permission and then she learns of the contract and remains silent, her silence is considered permission in the first case and ratification in the second, due to the indication of the situation, as previously explained in several contexts.
Source pages p. 921

Commentary
This passage expands on the legal maxim 'لا يُنسب إلى ساكت قول' (No speech is attributed to a silent person) which is maxim 57 of the Majalla. The principle is that silence is not automatically interpreted as speech, but it may be treated as such when the context necessitates a response. The text begins by stating the maxim and giving its rationale: silence is inherently ambiguous, and cannot be taken as consent or acknowledgment unless there is corroborating evidence. A clear example is given: if you see someone selling your property and you remain silent, you are not deemed to have consented; you can still reclaim it later. However, an exception is made for spouses and close relatives: their silence in such a sale is considered an acknowledgment of the seller's right, due to the close relationship that creates a strong presumption of knowledge and consent. This exception is based on istihsan (juristic preference) to prevent exploitation. The text also addresses the case of an impotent husband's wife: her long silence does not waive her right to seek a judicial divorce. The passage then defines 'معرض الحاجة' (a situation that requires explanation) as any context where speaking is necessary to avoid harm or deception, or where silence is customarily understood as an expression. Three applications are given: (a) a defendant's silence in court is treated as a denial, and if he remains silent when offered an oath, it is considered refusal leading to judgment against him; (b) a pre-emptor's silence after learning of a sale forfeits his pre-emption right, to prevent deceit; and (c) a virgin girl's silence in marriage matters is considered consent or ratification, as her modesty and custom make silence indicative of agreement. These furuat demonstrate how the maxim is applied across different areas of fiqh.

Key Terms
ساكت (sākit): A person who remains silent in a context where speech might be expected.
معرض الحاجة (maʿraḍ al-ḥājah): A situation where the necessity of speech arises, such as to avoid harm or deception, or where silence is customarily understood as expression.
استحسان (istiḥsān): Juristic preference; a method of reasoning that deviates from qiyas in favor of a more suitable ruling based on public interest or custom.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In which of the following cases would a person's silence be considered a legal expression according to the Hanafi maxim?
A) A person remains silent when seeing a stranger sell his property without permission.
B) A wife remains silent for years about her husband's impotence without seeking divorce.
C) A defendant remains silent when asked by the judge to respond to a claim.
D) A person remains silent when a friend sells his own property in the market.

Key Takeaway
Silence is inherently ambiguous and not legally binding, but when the context demands speech, silence can speak as consent or acknowledgment.

Silence in Context of Need: The Maxim and Its Applications
Explains a legal maxim with its definition, applications, and exception.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the maxim 'al-sukūt fī maʿraḍ al-ḥāja bayān' to identify when silence is considered expression in judicial, pre-emption, and marriage contexts, and distinguish the exception for the wife of an impotent man.

Core Idea
Silence is only legally binding as expression when context demands speech to avoid harm or when custom treats it as consent.

This lesson examines a powerful Hanafi maxim that treats silence as a form of expression, but only in specific situations. The passage from Mustafa Ahmad al-Zarqa's al-Madkhal al-Fiqhi al-'Amm defines the 'context of need' and provides three practical applications from different chapters of fiqh. It also highlights a critical exception: the wife of an impotent man. Understanding this maxim is essential for muftis who must infer consent or rejection from silence in daily fatwa work.

Guided Path
1
State the maxim and its scope
Begin by reciting the maxim in Arabic and English. Note its rank as a minor (sughra) universal maxim applicable across fiqh chapters where consent or declaration is required.
Maxim codified in Majalla Article 67.
2
Define 'context of need' (maʿraḍ al-ḥāja)
Analyze the author's definition: any situation where speaking is required to repel harm or deception, or where silence is customary expression. This definition sets the condition for the maxim to apply.
The exception proves the condition: the wife is not in a context of need.
3
Work through each furu' applying the maxim
For each of the three cases (defendant in court, pre-emptor, virgin bride), identify the context of need and explain why silence is treated as a specific expression (denial, acceptance, permission).
Notice the ratio legis: preventing harm or deception.
4
Identify the istithnā' and its governing maxim
Examine the exception: the wife's silence does not constitute consent to waive her right. The reason is absence of need—she may be waiting for treatment. The governing maxim is 'Harm must be removed' (al-ḍarar yuzāl).
This exception prevents the maxim from causing injustice.

والمراد بمعرض الحاجة الذي يكون فيه السكوت في حكم البيان والتعبير : كل موطن يلزم فيه التكلم لدفع ضرر أو غرر، أو يكون فيه السكوت طريقة عرفية للتعبير. وعلى هذا :

And likewise, if the wife of an impotent man remains silent for years, her silence is not considered consent that drops her right to judicial separation between her and her husband. And the meaning of 'context of need' in which silence is in the ruling of expression and declaration: every situation in which speaking is required to repel harm or deception, or in which silence is a customary method of expression. And upon this: a) If the judge asks the defendant what he says regarding the plaintiff's claim, and he remains silent, he is considered a denier of the claim, so the plaintiff is required to provide proof. And if he is unable to provide proof and requests an oath, and the oath is presented to the defendant, and he also remains silent without taking the oath or refusing, he is considered refusing the oath and judgment is passed against him, because the court's proceedings being halted by his speech harms the plaintiff. (1) The explanation of the meaning of pre-emption and the pre-emptor has already been given, so look to (F 7/23 footnote). b) Likewise, if the pre-emptor knows of the sale of property in which he has a right of pre-emption, and he remains silent regarding his request, his silence is considered acceptance dropping his pre-emption right, so that the pre-emptor does not intend to deceive the buyer by this silence until he builds or plants, then the pre-emptor requests taking the property. c) If a virgin girl remains silent when her guardian seeks her permission for marriage, or if the guardian marries her without her permission and then she learns of the contract and remains silent, her silence is considered permission in the first case and acceptance in the second due to the indication of the situation, as previously explained in several contexts: see F 7/3 and 10/69).
Source pages p. 922

Commentary
This passage expounds the legal maxim that silence in a context of need is considered as expression. The author first clarifies that this does not apply universally: the wife of an impotent man can remain silent for years without her silence being consent to drop her right to seek judicial separation, because she is not in a situation where speaking is required to avoid harm. The maxim applies only when there is a context of need (ma'rad al-haja): either speaking is necessary to prevent harm or deception, or silence is a customary way of expressing consent. Three applications are given. First, in judicial proceedings: if a defendant remains silent when asked to respond to a claim, he is treated as a denier, requiring the plaintiff to prove; if he then remains silent when the oath is offered, he is considered a refuser (nakil) and judgment goes against him, because his silence harms the plaintiff by delaying the court. Second, in pre-emption: if a pre-emptor learns of the sale but remains silent, his silence is deemed acceptance that forfeits his right, to prevent him from misleading the buyer into making improvements and then claiming the property. Third, in marriage: a virgin's silence when asked for her permission is consent, and her silence after being married without permission is ratification, because customarily a virgin may be shy to speak.

Key Terms
السكوت في معرض الحاجة بيان (al-sukūt fī maʿraḍ al-ḥāja bayān): The legal principle that silence in a situation requiring speech is considered as an explicit expression.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) His silence is disregarded and he retains his right to pre-emption.
B) His silence is considered acceptance, and he loses his right to pre-emption.
C) He must explicitly reject the sale; silence has no effect.
D) His silence is considered a request for more time.

Key Takeaway
Silence is treated as expression only when context demands speech or custom dictates it; otherwise, it carries no legal effect.

Probability Supported by Evidence Is Considered
Explains the maxim with furuat from testimony and confession.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the maxim 'probability supported by evidence is considered' to evaluate testimonies and confessions in Hanafi law, distinguishing it from baseless conjecture.

Core Idea
Evidence-backed probability overrides baseless conjecture in Hanafi law.

The Hanafi school distinguishes between mere conjecture and probability supported by circumstantial evidence. This lesson explores the maxim that such evidence-backed probability is legally recognized, impacting rulings on testimony and confessions. The examples from shahada and iqrar illustrate how entrenched suspicion invalidates actions.

Guided Path
1
Define the maxim and its core term
Understand the meaning of 'tamakkun al-tuhma' (entrenched suspicion) as probability supported by apparent circumstances, not mere conjecture. This is the basis of the maxim.
The maxim derives from al-Dabusi's Ta'sis al-Nazar.
2
Identify the condition for the maxim's application
Recognize that the probability must be supported by evidence (qaraina) from the apparent state of affairs. Without such support, it is baseless conjecture (tawahhum) and disregarded.
The maxim is a dabt (restriction) on the earlier maxim 'لا عبرة للتوهم'.
3
Analyze the furuat: testimony
Apply the maxim to testimony: relationships that create a strong likelihood of bias (spouses, ancestors/descendants, private employees) make the testimony inadmissible due to entrenched suspicion.
The relationship is the circumstantial evidence supporting the probability of partiality.
4
Analyze the furuat: confession in death sickness
Apply the maxim to confessions during marad al-mawt: confession to an heir is not enforceable without other heirs' consent, and confessed debts compete unfavorably with health debts, because death sickness creates a strong probability of favoritism.
The estate's narrowness and the timing of confession are circumstantial evidence.
5
Contrast with health confessions
Recognize the istithna: confessions made during health have no circumstantial evidence of collusion, so the maxim does not apply; they are fully enforceable.
This contrast reinforces the condition: evidence must support the probability.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
١٥/٨١ - ط - الا حجة مع الاحتمال الناشيء عن دليل (م/ ۷۳) أصل هذه القاعدة ما في تأسيس النظر للدبوسي (ص/١٩): إنَّ التهمة إذا تمكنت من فعل الفاعل حكم بفساد فعله». ومعنى تمكن التهمة أنَّ لها مؤيداً من ظاهر الحال وليست مجرد توهم
وعلى هذا لا تقبل شهادة الزوجين وشهادة الأصول والفروع بعضهم لبعض ولا شهادة الأجير الخاص لمستأجره لتمكن التهمة الناشئة عن علاقة قد تدفع إلى تحزب مريب يجب أن تتجرد الشهادة عنه.
- ولو أقر شخص في مرض موته لبعض ورثته بدين لا ينفذ إقراره إلا بتصديق باقي الورثة، لأن احتمال اتخاذ هذا الإقرار مطية لترجيح المُقَر له على غيره في الإرث هو احتمال قوي تدل عليه حالة مرض الموت.
·
ومثل ذلك ما لو أقرّ في مرض موته بدين يُزاحم بقية الديون الناشئة في حال الصحة، وتركته ضيّقة، فإنَّ ديون الصحة تكون ممتازة. أي أنها تستوفى قبل الديون التي ليس لها بينة سوى الإقرار في مرض الموت.
فلو كان الاحتمال الا دليل عليه لا عبرة له كما لو كان الإقرار في حال الصحة، فإنه تصرف طبيعي، فينفذ ولا تقدح فيه هذه الاحتمالات، لأنها عندئذ مجرد توهم ..
15/81 - T - 'Only a claim based on probability arising from evidence is considered' (Article 73). The origin of this rule is in Ta'sis al-Nazar by al-Dabusi (p. 19): 'When suspicion is entrenched in an action, the action is judged as invalid.' And the meaning of 'entrenched suspicion' is that it has support from the apparent circumstances and is not mere conjecture. And upon this, the testimony of spouses, and testimony of ascendants and descendants for each other is not accepted, nor the testimony of a special employee for his employer, due to the entrenched suspicion arising from a relationship that may lead to partisan bias from which testimony must be free. And if a person in his death sickness confesses a debt to one of his heirs, his confession is not enforceable except with the confirmation of the remaining heirs, because the probability that this confession is a means to favor the confessee over others in inheritance is a strong probability indicated by the state of death sickness. And similarly, if he confesses in his death sickness a debt that competes with other debts arising during health, and his estate is narrow, then the health debts are preferred, meaning they are satisfied before debts that have no evidence except the confession in death sickness. If the probability has no evidence, it is given no regard, as when the confession is made during health, for it is a natural act, so it is enforced and these probabilities do not harm it, because in that case they are mere conjecture.
Source pages p. 923

Commentary
This passage presents the corollary maxim to the previous one: while baseless conjecture is disregarded, a probability that is supported by evidence or circumstantial indicators is legally recognized. The author quotes al-Dabusi's Ta'sis al-Nazar: when suspicion is entrenched (i.e., supported by apparent circumstances), the act is judged invalid. This is applied in several areas. First, testimony is rejected when there is a relationship that creates a strong suspicion of bias: spouses testifying for each other, ascendants/descendants for each other, and a private employee for his employer, because such relationships may lead to forbidden partisanship. Second, a sick person's confession of a debt to an heir is not effective without the other heirs' confirmation, because the death sickness creates a strong probability that the confession is a device to favor that heir. Third, if a sick person confesses a debt that would compete with debts from health, the health debts are given priority because the confession during illness is suspect. The passage concludes by contrasting this with confessions made during health, where no such probability exists, so the confession is fully enforced. This maxim shows that only probabilities grounded in evidence have legal effect.

Key Terms
تمكن التهمة (tamakkun al-tuhma): That the suspicion has support from apparent circumstances and is not mere conjecture.
الإقرار في مرض الموت (al-iqrār fī maraḍ al-mawt): A confession made during a terminal illness.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In Hanafi law, why is a confession made during death sickness to an heir not enforceable without the confirmation of other heirs?
A) Because the heir is a minor.
B) Because there is a strong probability that the confession is a device to favor the heir over others.
C) Because the confession was made orally.
D) Because the dying person is not legally competent.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, only probabilities supported by circumstantial evidence (tamakkun al-tuhma) are given legal weight; baseless conjecture is disregarded.

6 min
Ignoring Baseless Probability in Legal Judgments
Explaining the rule that disregards baseless probability with examples.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi maxim 'al-ihtimal al-mawhum la ibrah lahu' to determine when a possibility should be disregarded in legal rulings.

Core Idea
A baseless probability (mawhum) never obstructs a ruling based on apparent certainty.

In legal rulings, not every possibility affects the outcome. The Hanafi school distinguishes between credible doubt and baseless conjecture. This lesson explores the maxim that disregards illusory probabilities and applies it to inheritance, insolvency, and testimony.

Guided Path
1
State the maxim and its meaning
Identify the maxim: 'الاحتمال الموهوم لا عبرة له' (baseless probability is disregarded). Understand that mawhum refers to a possibility with no supporting evidence.
Distinguish mawhum from shakk (doubt) and zann (strong probability).
2
Identify the first furua: inheritance
In faraid, if only certain heirs are known, the estate is distributed to them. The possibility of an unknown heir is mawhum and ignored.
This prevents indefinite delay in estate distribution.
3
Identify the second furua: insolvency
When creditors prove debts and witnesses state no other creditors, the present creditors are paid. The possibility of hidden creditors is mawhum.
This ensures timely payment without endless searches.
4
Identify the third furua: testimony
Trustworthy witnesses' testimony is accepted despite the theoretical possibility of error or falsehood. That possibility is mawhum.
This upholds the reliability of the judicial process.
5
Understand the relationship with 'certainty is not removed by doubt'
The complementary maxim 'اليقين لا يزول بالشك' reinforces that apparent certainty is maintained unless a credible doubt undermines it. Mawhum does not constitute such a doubt.
Together these maxims ensure stability in legal outcomes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الباب العاشر : القواعد الكلية في الفقه وقالوا: لا تعلم له وارثاً غيرهم يقضى لهم بالإرث، ولا عبرة لاحتمال ظهور وارث آخر، لأنَّ ذلك موهوم، فلا يعوق القضاء. - وكذلك لو أثبت الدائنون ديونهم على مفلس أو على تركته، وقال الشهود لا نعلم له غريماً آخر يعطى المال للحاضرين. - وكذا أمر الشهود الثقات : يُعتمد على شهادتهم ويقضى بها، ولا عبرة لاحتمال خطئهم أو كذبهم . توهم.
Chapter Ten: The Comprehensive Maxims in Fiqh. And they said: If no heir other than them is known, the inheritance is awarded to them, and no heed is paid to the possibility of another heir emerging, because that is illusory, so it does not prevent the judgment. - Similarly, if creditors prove their debts against an insolvent person or his estate, and the witnesses say we know of no other creditor, the money is given to those present. - And likewise, the matter of trustworthy witnesses: their testimony is relied upon and judged by it, and no heed is paid to the possibility of their error or lying. Illusion.
Source pages p. 923

Commentary
This passage introduces a key principle in the chapter on comprehensive maxims: baseless probability is not considered in legal rulings. The author provides three applications: (1) In inheritance, if only known heirs are present, the estate is distributed to them despite the theoretical possibility of an unknown heir. (2) In insolvency, if witnesses attest that there are no other creditors, the current creditors receive the assets. (3) Testimony of reliable witnesses is accepted despite the theoretical possibility of mistake or falsehood. The key point is that a mere improbable possibility ('wahm') does not obstruct a judgment based on apparent certainty.

Key Terms
موهوم (mawhum): A baseless possibility with no supporting evidence

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because the possibility is illusory (mawhum)
B) Because the known heirs have a prior right
C) Because the unknown heir cannot be found
D) Because inheritance must be distributed quickly

Key Takeaway
The maxim 'baseless probability is disregarded' is a fundamental Hanafi principle that prevents legal paralysis by ignoring improbable possibilities, as illustrated in inheritance, insolvency, and testimony.

The Maxim of Probability Supported by Evidence
Explaining the maxim and its applications in testimony and acknowledgments

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the maxim 'لا حجة مع الاحتمال الناشئ عن دليل' to identify when a probability arising from evidence renders an act invalid, and distinguish it from baseless probability.

Core Idea
Probability supported by evidence invalidates; baseless probability does not.

This lesson introduces a key legal maxim from the Hanafi school: probability arising from evidence nullifies the legal effect of an act. The maxim governs cases where suspicion (tuhma) is grounded in apparent circumstances, such as family ties or deathbed context. Understanding this maxim is crucial for muftis evaluating testimony or acknowledgments.

Guided Path
1
Identify the maxim and its origin
State the maxim and note its source from al-Dabusi's Ta'sis al-Nazar.
2
Understand the condition: probability must have supporting evidence
Distinguish between tuhma mutamakkinah (suspicion with evidence) and mere illusion.
3
Work through the furuat: testimony
Apply the maxim to spouses, parents-children, and private employee testimony.
4
Work through the furuat: deathbed acknowledgments
Apply the maxim to deathbed debt acknowledgment to an heir and competition with health debts.
5
Identify the istithna'
Note the exception when probability has no evidence (e.g., health acknowledgment); the act remains valid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
١٥/٨١ - ط - الا حجة مع الاحتمال الناشيء عن دليل (م/ ۷۳) أصل هذه القاعدة ما في تأسيس النظر للدبوسي (ص/١٩): إنَّ التهمة إذا تمكنت من فعل الفاعل حكم بفساد فعله». ومعنى تمكن التهمة أنَّ لها مؤيداً من ظاهر الحال وليست مجرد توهم. وعلى هذا لا تقبل شهادة الزوجين وشهادة الأصول والفروع بعضهم لبعض ولا شهادة الأجير الخاص لمستأجره لتمكن التهمة الناشئة عن علاقة قد تدفع إلى تحزب مريب يجب أن تتجرد الشهادة عنه. - ولو أقر شخص في مرض موته لبعض ورثته بدين لا ينفذ إقراره إلا بتصديق باقي الورثة، لأن احتمال اتخاذ هذا الإقرار مطية لترجيح المُقَر له على غيره في الإرث هو احتمال قوي تدل عليه حالة مرض الموت. · ومثل ذلك ما لو أقرّ في مرض موته بدين يُزاحم بقية الديون الناشئة في حال الصحة، وتركته ضيّقة، فإنَّ ديون الصحة تكون ممتازة. أي أنها تستوفى قبل الديون التي ليس لها بينة سوى الإقرار في مرض الموت. فلو كان الاحتمال الا دليل عليه لا عبرة ،له كما لو كان الإقرار في حال الصحة، فإنه تصرف طبيعي، فينفذ ولا تقدح فيه هذه الاحتمالات، لأنها عندئذ مجرد توهم ..
15/81 - T - No proof with probability arising from evidence (Article 73). The origin of this maxim is in Ta'sis al-Nazar by al-Dabusi (p. 19): 'When suspicion takes hold of an action of an agent, it is judged that his action is invalid.' The meaning of suspicion taking hold is that it has support from the apparent situation and is not mere illusion. On this basis, the testimony of spouses, and the testimony of ascendants and descendants for each other, and the testimony of a special employee for his employer are not accepted, because of the presence of suspicion arising from a relationship that may lead to a partiality from which testimony must be free. - And if a person acknowledges a debt to one of his heirs during his death illness, his acknowledgment is not effective except with the ratification of the remaining heirs, because the possibility of using this acknowledgment as a means to favor the acknowledged over others in inheritance is a strong possibility indicated by the state of death illness. Similarly, if he acknowledges a debt during death illness that competes with other debts arising in health, and his estate is narrow, then the health debts are privileged. That is, they are satisfied before the debts that have no evidence other than the acknowledgment in death illness. If the probability has no evidence, it is disregarded, like an acknowledgment in health, which is a natural act; it is effective and these probabilities do not invalidate it, because they are then mere illusion.
Source pages p. 923

Commentary
This passage discusses the maxim 'لا حجة مع الاحتمال الناشئ عن دليل' (No argument with probability arising from evidence). The foundation, from al-Dabusi, is that when a suspicion (tuhma) is established in an action due to supporting circumstantial evidence, the action is ruled invalid. The author gives applications: (1) Testimony between spouses, and between parents and children, is rejected due to the strong suspicion of partiality arising from family ties. Similarly, a private employee's testimony for his employer is rejected. (2) An acknowledgment of debt to an heir during death illness is ineffective without consent of other heirs because of the strong suspicion that it is a ploy to favor that heir. (3) Debts acknowledged during death illness are subordinate to debts arising in health when the estate is tight. The key distinction is that only probabilities supported by evidence (like the context of death illness) are considered; baseless probabilities are ignored, as in acknowledgments made in health.

Key Terms
تهمة (tuhma): Suspicion based on circumstantial evidence that affects the validity of an act
إقرار مرض الموت (iqrar fi marad al-mawt): Acknowledgment made during a death illness, which is subject to heightened scrutiny

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is the testimony of spouses to each other not accepted according to this maxim?
A) Because spouses are not trustworthy
B) Because of the strong suspicion of partiality arising from their relationship
C) Because they are considered the same entity
D) Because the Qur'an prohibits it

Key Takeaway
Probability arising from evidence invalidates legal acts; baseless probability is disregarded.

The Maxim of Manifestly Erroneous Assumptions
Explaining the maxim with definitions and furu‘

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the maxim 'لا عبرة بالظن البين خطوه' to cases of mistaken payment and distinguish it from cases of donative intent.

Core Idea
An action built on a false assumption is undone when the error is revealed.

In Hanafi fiqh, we often act on preponderant assumptions (zann), but if that assumption turns out to be clearly wrong, the ruling based on it collapses. This lesson unpacks the maxim 'No heed is paid to a manifestly erroneous assumption' (لا عبرة بالظن البين خطوه), defining key terms like zann, ghalib al-zann, and shakk. Through concrete examples like double payment of a debt, you'll see how the maxim operates and where it is restricted by the rule 'Matters are according to intentions'.

Guided Path
1
Define the three probability states
Identify and distinguish between zann (preponderant assumption), ghalib al-zann (very strong assumption), and shakk (equal doubt). Note which can be a basis for action in Hanafi law.
Zann is action-guiding; shakk is not; ghalib al-zann is stronger.
2
State the maxim and its literal meaning
Read the Arabic maxim 'لا عبرة بالظن البين خطوه' and its English equivalent. Understand that 'بين خطوه' means 'manifestly erroneous'.
The maxim voids any legal effect built on an assumption that later proves false.
3
Analyse the furu‘ (applications) in the text
Examine the two examples: (1) double payment by agent/guarantor, (2) payment under mistaken belief of obligation. For each, identify the assumption, the error, and the legal consequence (recovery).
The second payer recovers because his payment was based on a false assumption.
4
Identify the istithna’ (exception)
Note the exception: if the payment was made with donative intent (not based on assumption of obligation), the maxim does not apply; the ruling of gift governs.
This exception shows the interaction with the maxim 'al-umur bi-maqasidiha'.
5
Apply the maxim to a new case
Consider a scenario outside the text: someone pays zakat on the assumption his wealth reached nisab, but later finds it did not. Does he recover? Apply the maxim.
The maxim would allow recovery of the amount paid in error.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفصل (۸۱) شرح قواعد المجلة وتصنيفها ١٦/٨١ - ي - لا عبرة بالظن البين خطوه» (م/ ۷۲). الظن : هو اعتقاد الاحتمال الراجح الذي ظهر رجحانه على نقيضه بدليل معتبر. فإذا ازداد قوة حتى أصبح خلافه موهوماً : فهو غالب الظن. والشك : تساوي الاحتمالات دون رجحان لأحدها. ومعنى القاعدة : أنه إذا بني حكم واستحقاق على ظن ثم تبين خطوه بطل . - فلو دفع المدين الدين، ثم دفعه عنه وكيله أو كفيله جاهلاً أداء الأصيل، وكذا العكس يسترد الدافع الثاني ما دفع. - وكذا كل من دفع شيئاً على ظن وجوبه، أو صالح عن حق مدعى به عليه، ولم يكن قد أقرَّ به ثم تبين عدم الحق فله استرداد ما دفع . أما إذا لم يكن الدفع على ظن الوجوب، بل بقصد التبرع، فإنه يجري عليه حكم الهبة، ويكون عندئذ من فروع القاعدة الأولى الأمور بمقاصدها».
Chapter (81): Explanation of the Maxims of the Majalla and Their Classification. 16/81 - Y - No heed is paid to an assumption whose error is manifest (Article 72). Assumption (zann) is a belief of a preponderant probability whose preponderance over its opposite appears through a valid evidence. If it increases in strength until its opposite becomes illusory, then it is predominant assumption (ghalib al-zann). And doubt (shakk) is the equivalence of probabilities without preponderance of any. And the meaning of the maxim: That if a ruling or entitlement is built upon an assumption and then its error becomes clear, it becomes void. - So if the debtor pays the debt, and then his agent or guarantor pays it on his behalf, unaware of the principal's payment, and likewise the opposite, the second payer may recover what he paid. - And likewise, anyone who pays something on the assumption of its obligation, or settles a claim brought against him, and he had not acknowledged it, and then it becomes clear that there was no right, he may recover what he paid. But if the payment was not based on an assumption of obligation, but with the intention of donation, then the ruling of gift applies, and it is considered under the first maxim: 'Matters are according to their intentions.'
Source pages p. 924

Commentary
This passage, from the section explaining the Majalla's maxims, defines key terms: zann (assumption with preponderance), ghalib al-zann (strong assumption), and shakk (doubt). The maxim states that any ruling or right established on a false assumption is void when the error is realized. The author provides two applications: (1) Double payment of debt: if a debtor pays, then his agent or guarantor pays again in ignorance, the second payor can recover. (2) Payment under a mistaken belief of obligation: if someone pays or settles a claim thinking it was owed, but it later turns out it was not, he can recover. However, if he paid with donative intent, it is considered a gift and cannot be recovered, falling under the maxim 'al-umur bi-maqasidiha'.

Key Terms
ظن (zann): A belief of preponderant probability supported by valid evidence
غالب الظن (ghalib al-zann): A very strong assumption where the opposite is considered illusory
شك (shakk): Equal probability between two possibilities without preponderance

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person pays a debt on the assumption it is owed, but later discovers he already paid, can he recover the money?
A) Yes, because the assumption was erroneous
B) No, because payment is final
C) Only if the debtor agrees
D) No, because it was a gift

Key Takeaway
An action based on a manifestly erroneous assumption is void, but if the actor intended donation, the gift ruling applies and recovery is barred.

The Maxim of Customary Impossibility (الممتنع عادة كالممتنع حقيقة)
Explaining the maxim that what is customarily impossible is treated as actually impossible.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi maxim al-mumtani' 'ada ka al-mumtani' haqiqa to evaluate claims in litigation and identify when a claim is blocked by customary impossibility.

Core Idea
Customary impossibility is treated as real impossibility unless strong evidence proves the improbable.

This lesson explores a powerful legal maxim that governs the admissibility of claims in Hanafi courts. The maxim states that what is customarily impossible is treated as actually impossible. While rationally possible, such claims are rejected unless the claimant provides concrete proof of a legitimate source. Through two furuat (applications), you will see how this maxim operates in practice.

Guided Path
1
State the maxim and its scope
Understand that the maxim applies when a claim is highly improbable based on custom, even if theoretically possible.
Maxim: 'الممتنع عادة كالممتنع حقيقة'
2
Distinguish real from customary impossibility
Real impossibility (e.g., peer claiming paternity) is rejected outright; customary impossibility requires proving a source.
3
Identify the legal effect
The claim is not heard and evidence is not accepted unless the claimant proves a credible source.
Article 38 of the Majalla
4
Apply to first furu': poor person claiming huge sums
Without proof of inheritance or other legitimate acquisition, the claim is blocked.
5
Apply to second furu': trustee's unreasonable expenses
A trustee's claim of exorbitant expenses on waqf or minor's property is similarly rejected.
6
Note the exception
If the claimant provides strong evidence of a credible source, the claim may be heard.
The maxim is not absolute; it can be overcome

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
١٧/٨١ - ك - الممتنع عادة كالممتنع حقيقة» (م/ ۳۸). الممتنع حقيقة هو الذي لا يمكن وقوعه فهذا لا يقبل الادعاء به، بل يرفض، كمن ادعى على مساويه سناً أنه ابنه أو أبوه. والممتنع عادة هو الذي لا يعهد وقوعه وإن كان فيه احتمال عقلي بعيد. فلو ادعى شخص معروف بالفقر على آخر أموالاً جسيمة لا يُعرف أنه أصاب مثلها بإرث أو غيره لا تُسمع دعواه ولا تقبل له بينة، مالم يثبت مصدراً لهذا المال. وكذا لو ادعى المتولي أو الوصي أنه أنفق على عقار الوقف أو القاصر مبالغ غير محتملة فإنه لا يصدق ولا تقبل بينته .
17/81 - K - What is customarily impossible is like what is actually impossible (Article 38). That which is actually impossible is that which cannot occur, so it is not accepted as a claim; rather it is rejected, like someone claiming that a person of similar age is his son or father. And what is customarily impossible is that which is not habitually known to occur, even though there is a remote rational possibility. So if a person known to be poor claims from another huge sums of money that are not known for him to have obtained through inheritance or otherwise, his lawsuit is not heard and his evidence is not accepted, unless he proves a source for this money. Also, if a trustee or guardian claims that he spent on a waqf property or a minor unreasonably large amounts, he is not believed and his evidence is not accepted.
Source pages p. 924

Commentary
This maxim distinguishes between two types of impossibility: real impossibility (like a peer claiming paternity) and customary impossibility (like a poor person claiming large debts). The latter, though theoretically possible, is so unlikely in practice that the law treats it as impossible. The author gives two applications: (1) A claim by a known poor person against another for huge sums is not entertained without proof of a legitimate source. (2) A trustee's claim of exorbitant expenses on waqf or minor's property is rejected unless credible.

Key Terms
ممتنع حقيقة (mumtani' haqiqa): Something that is factually impossible to occur
ممتنع عادة (mumtani' 'ada): Something that is customarily improbable, though rationally possible

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is a poor person's claim of a large debt against another not accepted?
A) Because it is impossible in reality
B) Because it is customarily impossible and no source is shown
C) Because the poor cannot have debts
D) Because the law does not protect the poor

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi maxim 'al-mumtani' 'ada ka al-mumtani' haqiqa' protects the judicial process by rejecting improbable claims unless credible evidence establishes the unlikely event.

The Maxim of Clearly Mistaken Conjecture and Its Applications
Explanation of maxim with definitions and examples of restitution

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the maxim 'لا عبرة بالظن البين خطوه' to cases of mistaken payment and distinguish it from cases of voluntary donation.

Core Idea
A mistaken payment based on false conjecture must be returned, unless it was intended as a gift.

This lesson explores a key Hanafi legal maxim from the Majalla that protects against unjust enrichment when payments are made based on mistaken beliefs. Understanding this maxim helps muftis resolve cases of double payment and erroneous settlements. We will break down its terms, applications, and an important exception.

Guided Path
1
Define the Key Terms
Identify and understand 'zann' (conjecture), 'ghalib al-zann' (overwhelming conjecture), and 'shakk' (doubt) as defined in the text.
These terms are foundational for applying the maxim correctly.
2
State the Maxim
Read the maxim 'لا عبرة بالظن البين خطوه' and grasp its literal meaning: no legal effect is given to a conjecture that is clearly mistaken.
The maxim is from Article 72 of the Majalla.
3
Examine the Furuat (Applications)
Apply the maxim to the two cases given: (1) an agent or surety pays a debt already paid by the principal, (2) someone pays a claim mistakenly believed to be due.
In both cases, the second payer recovers what he paid.
4
Identify the Istithna' (Exception)
Note the exception: if the payment was intended as a gift (تبرع), it is a valid donation and cannot be recovered.
This exception is governed by the maxim 'الأمور بمقاصدها' (Acts are judged by intentions).
5
Recognize the Interplay of Maxims
Understand that when intention is present, the maxim of intentions may override the current maxim. The mufti must assess the payor's intention.
Always check whether the payment was made under a mistaken obligation or as a voluntary gift.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفصل (۸۱) شرح قواعد المجلة وتصنيفها
١٦/٨١ - ي - لا عبرة بالظن البين خطوه» (م/ ۷۲).
الظن : هو اعتقاد الاحتمال الراجح الذي ظهر رجحانه على نقيضه بدليل معتبر. فإذا ازداد قوة حتى أصبح خلافه موهوماً : فهو غالب الظن.
والشك : تساوي الاحتمالات دون رجحان لأحدها.
ومعنى القاعدة : أنه إذا بني حكم واستحقاق على ظن ثم تبين خطوه
- فلو دفع المدين الدين، ثم دفعه عنه وكيله أو كفيله جاهلاً أداء الأصيل، وكذا العكس يسترد الدافع الثاني ما دفع.
- وكذا كل من دفع شيئاً على ظن وجوبه، أو صالح عن حق مدعى به عليه، ولم يكن قد أقر به ثم تبين عدم الحق فله استرداد ما دفع . أما إذا لم يكن الدفع على ظن الوجوب، بل بقصد التبرع، فإنه يجري عليه حكم الهبة، ويكون عندئذ من فروع القاعدة الأولى الأمور بمقاصدها».
Chapter 81: Explanation of the Maxims of the Majalla and Their Classification. 16/81 - Ya - No regard is paid to a conjecture that is clearly mistaken. Conjecture is a belief of a preponderant probability whose preponderance over its opposite has become apparent by a valid evidence. If it increases in strength until its opposite becomes illusory, then it is overwhelming conjecture. Doubt is equality of probabilities without preponderance of any. The meaning of the rule: if a ruling or entitlement is built on conjecture and then its error becomes apparent: if the debtor pays a debt, then his agent or surety pays it for him unaware of the principal's payment, and likewise the opposite, the second payer recovers what he paid. Likewise, anyone who pays something due to a conjecture of its obligation, or settles a claim made against him, and he had not admitted it, then it becomes clear there is no right, he may recover what he paid. But if the payment was not due to a conjecture of obligation, but with the intention of donation, then the ruling of gift applies, and it becomes a branch of the first maxim 'Matters are determined by intentions'.
Source pages p. 924

Commentary
This passage presents a legal maxim from the Majalla, explaining its key terms and applications. It opens by defining 'conjecture' (ظن) as a preponderant belief supported by evidence, and distinguishes it from 'overwhelming conjecture' (غالب الظن) and 'doubt' (شك). The maxim states that if a legal action is based on conjecture and later the error becomes clear, the action is reversed. The author gives two furuat: first, if a debtor pays his debt and then his agent or surety unknowingly pays the same debt, the second payer can reclaim his payment. Second, if someone pays something believing it obligatory or settles a claim without admission, and then discovers no obligation existed, he can recover. An exception is when the payment was intended as a gift—then it is a donation and falls under the maxim 'Acts are judged by intentions'. This demonstrates the Hanafi principle of restoring rights when based on mistaken belief.

Key Terms
الظن (al-zann): A belief in a preponderant probability supported by valid evidence; its opposite is less likely but possible
الشك (al-shakk): Equality of probabilities without preponderance
غالب الظن (ghalib al-zann): Overwhelming conjecture, where the opposite is considered remote and illusory

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling if a debtor pays his debt, and then his agent pays the same debt to the creditor unaware of the debtor's payment?
A) The second payment is considered a valid gift
B) The agent can recover his payment from the creditor
C) The debtor must repay the agent
D) The payment is forfeited

Key Takeaway
A payment made based on a mistaken belief that it was owed can be recovered, unless the payor intended it as a gift, in which case it is a valid donation.

8 min
Sub-Rule: Harm is Repelled as Much as Possible
Explains a subsidiary qa'ida and its furuat in public and private law.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the sub-maxim 'Harm is repelled as much as possible' to identify proactive harm prevention measures in public and private law, and distinguish its scope from the parent maxim 'Harm must be eliminated'.

Core Idea
Prevent harm before it strikes – obligation limited only by capacity.

The maxim 'Harm is repelled as much as possible' (الضرر يدفع بقدر الإمكان) is a proactive corollary of the major rule 'Harm must be eliminated'. It obligates taking all sufficient measures to prevent harm before it occurs, as prevention is better than cure. This lesson unpacks its applications in public interest (jihad, penalties, blocking means) and private rights (shuf'ah, hajr).

Guided Path
1
Identify the rule and its scope
Recognize that this sub-maxim mandates proactive prevention, not just removal of existing harm. Note the qualifier 'as much as possible' which limits obligation to capacity.
The rule is Article 31 of the Majallah.
2
Distinguish public vs private applications
Categorize the furuat given: public (jihad, penalties, sadd al-dhara'i) and private (shuf'ah, hajr). Understand that the rule operates in both spheres.
Public applications focus on collective security; private on individual rights.
3
Connect to parent maxim
See how this rule operationalizes the broader qa'ida 'Harm must be eliminated' by adding the capacity limitation. The parent maxim removes existing harm; this one prevents future harm.
Both are part of the same legal framework.

What branches from these rules. 19/81 - A - 'Harm is repelled as much as possible' (Art. 31). This rule expresses the obligation to repel harm before it occurs, by all sufficient and capable means, in accordance with the rule of unrestricted interests (masalih mursalah) and shariah policy (siyasah shar'iyyah). Because prevention is better than cure, and that is as much as possible, because legal obligation is according to capacity. So in the field of public interests: Jihad is legislated to repel the evil of enemies, penalties are obligatory to suppress crime and maintain internal security, and blocking the means of corruption and its doors from all types is obligatory, and other necessary measures to repel evil and prevent it. And in the field of private rights: The right of pre-emption (shuf'ah) is legislated, among its objectives to repel the harm of bad neighbors. And guardianship (hajr) over the foolish is legislated to repel the harm of his bad dispositions from himself.
Source pages p. 927

Commentary
This passage introduces a subsidiary maxim derived from the major rule 'Harm must be eliminated'. The maxim 'Harm is repelled as much as possible' (الضرر يدفع بقدر الإمكان) is Article 31 of the Majallah. The author explains that this rule mandates proactive prevention of harm before it occurs, using all sufficient means, limited only by capacity. The rationale is that prevention is better than cure, and Islamic law only obliges within ability. The passage then applies this to two fields: (1) Public interests: jihad against external aggression, criminal penalties for internal security, and blocking the means (sadd al-dhara'i) to corruption. (2) Private rights: the right of pre-emption (shuf'ah) to protect against a bad neighbor, and financial guardianship (hajr) over a spendthrift to protect himself and his family. These applications illustrate how the law mandates proactive measures within practical limits to prevent harm.

Key Terms
الضرر يدفع بقدر الإمكان (al-darar yudfa' bi-qadr al-imkan): Harm is repelled as much as possible; a sub-maxim mandating proactive prevention within capacity.
المصالح المرسلة (al-masalih al-mursalah): Unrestricted interests that are not explicitly regulated by scripture but are considered in legislation for public benefit
سد الذرائع (sadd al-dhara'i): Blocking the means that lead to harm or forbidden things

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Harm must be prevented before it occurs, limited only by one's capacity — this proactive duty is a cornerstone of Hanafi public and private law.

Choosing the Lesser Evil and Balancing Harms
Two parallel maxims about choosing lesser harm and greater mischief

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the maxim 'Choosing the lesser of two evils' to resolve conflicting harms in Hanafi fiqh and construct a fatwa using the framework of harm prioritization.

Core Idea
When two harms conflict, the greater harm is avoided by committing the lesser one.

This lesson introduces two closely related Hanafi legal maxims that guide decision-making when no option is harm-free. These maxims are essential for a mufti facing real-world dilemmas where avoiding all harm is impossible. Through the examples provided, you will learn how to weigh competing harms and determine the permissible course of action.

Guided Path
1
State the Maxim in Arabic and English
Read the two maxims carefully: 'يختار أهون الشرين' and 'إذا تعارض مفسدتان روعي أعظمهما ضررا بارتكاب أخفهما'. Understand that they are effectively the same principle expressed differently.
2
Identify the Scope of the Maxim
Recognize that this maxim applies across all chapters of fiqh where a conflict of harms or prohibitions arises, especially in cases of necessity, duress, and competing obligations.
The author notes that these two rules are in the meaning of the preceding rule (which is likely 'الضرر الأشد يُزال بالضرر الأخف').
3
Apply the Maxim to the Furu' Cases
Work through the two examples: (1) cutting open a dead pregnant woman's belly to save a viable fetus; (2) remaining silent about evil when speaking out would cause greater harm. For each, identify the two competing harms and state why the lesser harm is chosen.
The harm of cutting the corpse or remaining silent is lesser than the harm of losing the fetus or causing public disorder.
4
Relate to the Parallel Maxim 'الضرر الأشد يُزال بالضرر الأخف'
Compare the maxims: 'Choosing the lesser evil' focuses on which harmful act to commit, while 'severe harm is removed by lesser harm' focuses on the removal of an existing harm. Understand the nuanced difference in application.
Both share the same underlying principle of harm prioritization.
5
Evaluate Potential Istithna'at (Exceptions)
Consider scenarios where the maxim might not apply, e.g., if the 'lesser harm' is itself a major sin that cannot be justified, or if the greater harm is uncertain. Reflect on the role of ghalabat al-zann (prevailing presumption) in assessment.
The qawida panel indicates no istithna' in the text, but in practice, the maxim is bounded by other qawa'id.

And the permissibility of remaining silent about disapproving acts if speaking against them would result in a greater harm.

Commentary
This passage presents two additional maxims that closely align with the previous one about removing severe harm with lesser harm. The first maxim, 'The lesser of two evils is chosen,' is a well-known principle that applies when one must choose between two harmful options. The second maxim states that when two evils conflict, one considers the greater harm and avoids it by committing the lesser. The author notes that both are essentially the same as the previous rule and gives two Hanafi applications: (1) It is permissible to cut open a dead pregnant woman's belly to try to save the fetus, because the harm of cutting the corpse (which is forbidden normally) is lesser than the harm of losing a potentially living child. (2) It is permissible to remain silent about a wrongdoing if speaking out would cause a greater harm, such as public disorder or personal danger. This reflects the principle of weighing consequences in commanding good and forbidding evil.

Key Terms
أهون الشرين (ahwan al-sharayn): The lesser of two evils or two harms, which is to be chosen when no option is harm-free.
مفسدتان (mufsidatan): Two harmful or corrupting matters; two prohibitions or harms that conflict.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi legal tradition permits committing the lesser harm to avoid a greater harm, provided the conflict is genuine and the assessment of harm is objective.

When Preventer and Requirer Conflict: The Preventer Prevails (Unless Stronger Requirer)
Explaining the maxim with applications from partnership, bequest, agency, and witness accreditation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the maxim 'If the preventer and the requirer conflict, the preventer is given priority' to derive rulings in mu'amalat cases and identify exceptions when the requirer is stronger.

Core Idea
When legal reasons demand opposite outcomes, the preventer (mani') blocks the requirer (muqtadi) — unless the requirer is stronger, as in necessity.

This lesson explores a fundamental Hanafi legal maxim that resolves conflicts between a legal preventer (mani') and a legal requirer (muqtadi). The maxim states that the preventer prevails in most cases, because warding off evil takes precedence over bringing benefit. However, as you will see, this maxim is not absolute; when the requirer is stronger, it may override the preventer. We will study four practical applications from partnership, bequests, deposits, and witness credibility to internalize how this maxim operates in concrete cases.

Guided Path
1
State the maxim in Arabic and English
Identify the exact phrasing of the maxim as given in the passage. This is an intermediate (wusta) maxim rooted in the principle 'Warding off evil takes precedence over bringing benefit.'
Arabic: إذا تعارض المانع والمقتضي يُقدم المانع
2
Identify the underlying rationale
The maxim is derived from the overarching principle that preventing harm (mafsada) is prioritized over securing benefit (maslaha). This rationale is explicitly mentioned in the passage.
The passage states: 'because warding off evil takes precedence over bringing benefit.'
3
Work through each furu' (application)
For each of the four cases, identify the muqtadi (requirer) and the mani' (preventer). Explain why the preventer prevails in that specific scenario.
Cases: partnership harm, deathbed confession, deposit agent, witness accreditation.
4
Identify the crucial exception (istithna')
Note the qualification at the end: when the requirer is greater (e.g., necessity, reconciliation), the requirer prevails. The passage mentions the example of lying to reconcile disputants.
Exception governed by the maxim 'Necessities permit prohibited things.'
5
Apply the maxim to a new scenario
Practice by recognizing a preventer/requirer conflict in an unfamiliar case from mu'amalat and determining the ruling, including whether the exception applies.
Test with scenario: starved person eating pork.

٢٧/٨١ - إذا تعارض المانع والمقتضي يُقدم المانع (م/٤٦). أي إذا كان للشيء أو العمل محاذير تستلزم منعه، ودواع تقتضي تسويغه يرجح منعه، لأن درء المفاسد مقدم على جلب المصالح كما سلف بيانه في المادة السابقة.
وعلى هذا الأساس:

۲ - وإذا أقرَّ الشخص في مرض موته لأحد ورثته ولأجنبي بدين أو عين مشتركاً لم ينفذ في حق الأجنبي أيضاً لوجود مانع النفاذ في حق الوارث.
٣ - ولو زعم الشخص أنه وكيل المالك المودع بقبض العين الوديعة، ولا بينة له على الوكالة، فأقر الوديع له بالوكالة لا يُلزم بدفع الوديعة إليه، وإن كان إقراره يقتضي إلزامه بالتسليم، لأن حق المالك المودع في العين يقتضي عدم تسليمها لاحتمال إنكاره التوكيل كما تقدم.
٤ - وقالوا في تزكية الشاهد: إذا وثقه بعض المزكين وجرحه بعض، أي طعن في صدقه وعدالته يرجّح جانب الجرح، فيرد القاضي شهادته.
ملاحظة: إن هذه القاعدة مقيدة بما إذا لم يكن المقتضي أعظم من المانع. فإن كان أعظم يرجح المقتضي، إذ قلما يخلو أمر من محذور يكون عدمه أحسن لو أمكن. وإنما العبرة في الأمر والنهي التشريعي لغلبة أحد الضدين: النفع أو الضرر والخير أو الشر، على الآخر. ولذا جاز للوسيط بين المتخاصمين أن يكذب للإصلاح بينهما. وعلى هذا الأساس أيضاً بني في الشرع حكم الاضطرار، ووضعت فيه قاعدة أن الضرورات تبيح المحظورات.
Chapter (81) Explanation of the Maxims of the Majalla and Their Classification. 27/81 - If the preventer and the requirer conflict, the preventer is given priority (Art. 46). That is, if for a thing or action there are harmful aspects that necessitate its prohibition, and motivations that require its permissibility, its prohibition is given weight, because warding off evil takes precedence over bringing benefit, as explained in the previous article. On this basis: 1 - A partner is prevented from disposing of the common property in a way that harms his partner, because the right of his partner is a preventer even if his own right is a requirer. Similarly, one of the two owners of the lower or upper floor in multi-story buildings. 2 - If a person in his death sickness confesses to one of his heirs and to a stranger regarding a debt or property jointly, it does not take effect as to the stranger as well due to the existence of a preventer of effectiveness regarding the heir. 3 - If a person claims that he is the agent of the depositor for receiving the deposited item, and he has no evidence of agency, and the depositee acknowledges his agency, the depositee is not obliged to hand over the deposit to him, even though his acknowledgment requires him to deliver, because the right of the depositor in the item requires not handing it over due to the possibility of his denial of the agency, as previously mentioned. 4 - They said regarding the accreditation of a witness: If some of those accrediting certify him and some discredit him, i.e., cast doubt on his truthfulness and integrity, the side of discredit is given weight, so the judge rejects his testimony. Note: This maxim is restricted to cases where the requirer is not greater than the preventer. If it is greater, the requirer is given weight, since few matters are free from a harmful aspect whose absence would be more beneficial if possible. The consideration in legislative command and prohibition is the predominance of one of the two opposites: benefit or harm, good or evil, over the other. Therefore, it is permissible for a mediator between disputants to lie for the purpose of reconciliation. On this basis, the ruling of necessity is established in Islamic law, and the maxim 'Necessities permit prohibited things' is laid down.
Source pages p. 932

Commentary
This passage is an exposition of the Hanafi legal maxim: 'If a preventer (mani') and a requirer (muqtadi) conflict, the preventer is given priority.' The author explains that when a matter has both harmful aspects (prohibiting it) and beneficial aspects (permitting it), the prohibition is given weight because warding off evil takes precedence over bringing benefit. He then gives four applications: (1) A partner cannot use common property to harm his co-owner; (2) A deathbed confession to an heir and a stranger fails fully because the heir's right prevents enforcement; (3) An acknowledgment of agency does not compel delivery of the deposit because the depositor's right prevents it; (4) In witness accreditation, if some certify and some discredit, the discredit prevails. Finally, a crucial qualification is added: this maxim applies only when the requirer is not stronger. If the requirer is stronger (e.g., necessity or reconciliation), it may override the preventer.

Key Terms
مانع (mani'): A legal preventer that blocks the effectiveness of a right or ruling.
مقتضي (muqtadi): A legal requirer that demands a certain ruling or effect.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi maxim 'If the preventer and the requirer conflict, the preventer is given priority,' when would the requirer prevail?
A) Never; the preventer always prevails.
B) When the requirer is stronger, e.g., in cases of necessity.
C) Only in matters of worship (ibadat).
D) When both are equal.

Key Takeaway
The preventer prevails over the requirer unless the requirer is stronger, as in necessity or reconciliation.

The Maxim 'The Old is Left as It Was' and Its Applications
Explaining the maxim with applications from property rights and easements

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the maxim 'The old is left as it was' (al-qadīm yutraku ʿalā qadamihī) to cases of ancient easements and distinguish its exception for old defects in sales.

Core Idea
Long-standing possession of lawful facilities presumes a right; only a proven right can remove it.

This lesson unpacks a powerful Hanafi maxim that protects ancient, unchallenged possession of property facilities. You will learn how the maxim operates in property law, its evidence from Abu Yusuf's al-Kharaj, and a critical exception: the old defect in a sale, which triggers a different rule. By the end, you will be able to apply the maxim correctly in mufti scenarios.

Guided Path
1
Define 'old' as used in the maxim
Identify what 'al-qadīm' means in this context: a situation whose origin is unknown at the time of dispute — it has been there 'since before memory'.
This is a key legal definition that differs from ordinary usage.
2
State the maxim's legal effect
The maxim establishes a presumption: ancient possession of a right or facility is evidence that it was acquired legitimately. Therefore, the possession is left undisturbed.
The presumption is rebuttable only with clear proof of illegality.
3
Apply the maxim to property facilities
Work through the examples in the passage: ancient drainpipes, water channels, cesspits, passages, or beams resting on a neighbor's wall. The neighbor cannot remove them; the owner has the right to maintain them.
The key is that the facility must be originally lawful.
4
Identify the exception for old defects in sales
Note that 'old' here means the defect existed before delivery (even if it occurred between contract and delivery). This exception allows the buyer to rescind the sale.
This is an istithnā' — the maxim does not apply here; a different rule (al-kharāj bi al-damān) governs.
5
Integrate the maxim into fatwa practice
As a mufti, when asked about an ancient easement, you would apply this maxim to protect the possessor unless the claimant provides solid proof of an original wrong. For an old defect in a sale, you would instead apply the rules of khiyār al-ʿayb (option of defect).
The maxim's authority comes from its recognition in Hanafi texts and from the principle of certainty (al-yaqīn lā yazūlu bi al-shakk).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
٢٨/٨١ - القديم يُترك على قدمه (م/٦). القديم في هذا المقام هو ما لا يوجد وقت التنازع فيه من أدرك مبدأه. والمراد بهذه القاعدة أن ما كان في أيدي الناس أو تحت تصرفاتهم قديماً من أشياء ومنافع ومرافق مشروعة في أصلها يبقى لهم كما قدمه دليلاً على أنه حق قائم بطريق مشروع. ويعتبر وعلى هذا الأساس يقرر أبو يوسف في كتاب «الخراج» أنه: «لا ينزع شيء من يد أحد إلا بحق ثابت معروف». فلو كان لدار إنسان ميزاب على دار غيره أو كان له مسيل أو بالوعة أو ممر في أرض غيره، أو تحميل الجذوع داره على جدار جاره من القديم، فأراد ذلك الغير إزالته فليس له ذلك، بل يحق لصاحبه إبقاؤه ولو (١). بخلاف العيب القديم الذي يظهر في المبيع ويجيز للمشتري فسخ البيع، فإن المراد بالقديم هناك أن يكون موجوداً في المبيع وهو في يد البائع قبل تسليمه للمشتري: ولو أنه قد حدث بين العقد والقبض.
28/81 - The old is left as it was (Art. 6). 'Old' in this context is what has no known beginning at the time of dispute. The meaning of this maxim is that what has been in people's hands or under their disposal from ancient times, of things, benefits, and facilities that were originally lawful, remains theirs, and is considered evidence that it is a right established by lawful means. On this basis, Abu Yusuf rules in his book 'al-Kharaj': 'Nothing is taken from anyone's hand except with a proven, known right.' So if a person's house has a drainpipe on another's house, or has a water channel, or a cesspit, or a passage on another's land, or the beams of his house rest on his neighbor's wall from ancient times, and that other wants to remove it, he has no right to do so; rather, the owner has the right to keep it. Except for the old defect that appears in a sold item and gives the buyer the right to rescind the sale, for 'old' there means that it existed in the item while in the seller's hand before delivery to the buyer, even if it occurred between the contract and delivery.
Source pages p. 933

Commentary
This passage explains the maxim 'The old is left as it was' (al-qadīmu yutraku ʿalā qadamihī). 'Old' refers to a situation whose origin is not known at the time of dispute. The maxim establishes that long-standing possession or use of property, benefits, or facilities that were originally lawful is presumed to be based on a legitimate right. Thus, one cannot be dispossessed without clear proof. Imam Abu Yusuf in his book 'al-Kharaj' states that nothing should be taken from anyone except with a well-known, proven right. Applications: easements such as drainpipes, water channels, cesspits, passages, or beams resting on a neighbor's wall, if they are ancient, cannot be removed by the neighbor. The owner has the right to maintain them. However, the term 'old' has a different meaning in the context of defects in a sale: there it means the defect existed before the sale, giving the buyer the right to return the item.

Key Terms
القديم (al-qadīm): What has no known beginning at the time of dispute; ancient practice or possession.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Based on the passage, what is the Hanafi ruling for an ancient drainpipe that has been used for decades on a neighbor's land?
A) The neighbor can remove it because the land is his property.
B) The owner of the drainpipe must remove it if the neighbor requests.
C) The owner of the drainpipe has the right to keep it; the neighbor cannot remove it.
D) The case must be referred to the judge for a decision based on equity.

Key Takeaway
Ancient lawful possession of facilities is protected unless the challenger brings clear proof of an original wrong.

The Maxim 'The Old is Left as It Was' and Its Constraint
Explains a legal maxim with its constraint, examples, and exception.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the maxim by evaluating the balance between the beneficial factor (muqtada) and the harmful factor (mani'), and identify istithna'at where the maxim does not apply.

Core Idea
The old is presumed legitimate, but only if the benefit of keeping it outweighs the harm.

In this lesson, we examine one of the Majalla's universal maxims: 'The old is left as it was.' This maxim is widely applied in property and easement disputes. However, it is not absolute—it operates only when the beneficial factor (muqtada) of preserving the old is greater than the harmful factor (mani'). If the harm from keeping the old outweighs its benefit, the maxim is overridden. We will explore its definition, its constraint, its applications, and its exceptions.

Guided Path
1
Define 'al-qadim' and understand the maxim's scope
Identify what counts as 'old' (whose beginning is unknown) and the maxim's presumption of legitimate origin. The maxim applies to things, benefits, and facilities that are originally legitimate and have been in people's hands from time immemorial.
Refer to the definition: 'what is not known at the time of dispute'.
2
Apply the constraint: balance muqtada vs. mani'
Evaluate the examples (spout, drain, beams) and see how the maxim applies when muqtada > mani' (i.e., benefit of keeping outweighs harm of removal). But if the harm of keeping is greater, the maxim is overridden.
The passage gives a mediator lying for reconciliation as an example where benefit outweighs the prohibition.
3
Identify istithna'at: the exception of original harm
Recognize that if the old thing is originally illegitimate (e.g., harmful to the public), it must be removed regardless of age, governed by the maxim 'al-darar la yakunu qadiman'.
This exception prevents the misuse of the maxim to perpetuate harm.
